## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models acceleration in a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv/dt depends on velocity v and time t. The nonlinearity may arise from anharmonic restoring forces (Duffing-type), nonlinear damping (Van der Pol-type), or combinations thereof, with position implicitly encoded through time-dependent sinusoidal functions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring via time: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) (harmonic oscillator acceleration as sinusoidal function of time)
- Linear damping plus restoring: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (damped harmonic oscillator)
- Cubic velocity nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (nonlinear damping term)
- Van der Pol type: dv_dt = c0 * v * sin(c1 * t)**2 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (nonlinear damping with position-dependent term via time)
- Duffing restoring force via time: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * sin(c1 * t)**3 (cubic restoring force expressed through time)
- Quadratic velocity damping: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * v * abs(v) (drag-like nonlinear damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Velocity-dependent restoring: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * v**2 * sin(c3 * t) (cross-coupling of velocity and position)
- Combined nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * sin(c1 * t)**3 + c3 * v + c4 * v**3 (Duffing + Rayleigh combined)
- Parametric excitation: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * sin(c3 * t) (parametrically driven oscillator)
- Mathieu-type: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (parametric modulation of damping)
- Polynomial velocity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**2 + c2 * v**3 + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (general polynomial nonlinearity in velocity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Nonlinear damping → odd-power velocity terms (c*v**3, c*v**5) preserve time-reversal symmetry properties
- Anharmonic restoring force → cubic or higher odd-power sinusoidal terms in time: sin(ωt)**3 from Duffing-type nonlinearity
- Self-sustained oscillation → terms like (1 - v**2)*v or (1 - sin²(ωt))*v indicating amplitude-dependent damping sign change
- Position reconstructed from time → sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) substitutes for displacement x when only t is available
- Frequency mixing in nonlinear systems → multiple sinusoidal terms with harmonically related frequencies (ω, 3ω, 5ω)
- Energy-dependent behavior → acceleration terms proportional to v**2 * sin(c*t) coupling kinetic energy to restoring force
- Limit cycle dynamics → balance between negative linear damping (c*v with c>0) and positive cubic damping (c*v**3 with c<0)

GT Equivalence Verification (PO24)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*log(Abs(v) + c1)
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT: `-0.0834*v**3 - 0.9954*log(Abs(v) + 1) + 0.7824*sin(t)`

The key components of the GT are:
1. A `sin(t)` term
2. A `v**3` term
3. A `log(Abs(v) + 1)` term - this is the crucial non-polynomial, non-trigonometric term

Let me analyze the candidates. The critical question is whether any candidate can reproduce the `log(Abs(v) + 1)` term.

**Candidates with `sqrt(c1 + v**2)` (1-22):** The function `sqrt(c1 + v**2)` is an even function of v, while `log(Abs(v) + 1)` is also even in v. However, `sqrt(c1 + v**2)` behaves like `|v|` for large v, while `log(Abs(v)+1)` grows logarithmically. These are fundamentally different functions and cannot be made equivalent. Even with polynomial corrections (v**3, v**5, etc.), you cannot turn a square root into a logarithm.

**Candidates with polynomial terms only (21, 26-49 etc.):** Pure polynomials in v (v, v**2, v**3, v**5) cannot reproduce `log(Abs(v)+1)`.

**Candidates with `exp(c*v**2)` (2, 25, 37):** Exponential functions cannot reproduce logarithmic behavior.

**Candidates with `cos(c*v**2)` (39):** Cannot reproduce log.

**Candidate 24:** `c0*sin(c1*t + c2) + c3*v + c4*v**3 + c5*v**2 + c6*v**5 + c7*log(c8*exp(c9*v) + 1)`

This is very interesting! Let me analyze `c7*log(c8*exp(c9*v) + 1)`.

If c9 → 0, then exp(c9*v) ≈ 1 + c9*v, so log(c8*(1+c9*v) + 1) = log(c8 + 1 + c8*c9*v). This gives a logarithm of a linear function of v, not log(|v|+1).

For the GT we need `log(Abs(v) + 1)`. The expression `log(c8*exp(c9*v) + 1)` is a softplus-like function. For large positive c9*v, it behaves like c9*v + log(c8). For large negative c9*v, it approaches log(1) = 0. This is fundamentally asymmetric and cannot match `log(Abs(v)+1)` which is symmetric (even function).

However, we also have `c3*v + c5*v**2` terms. Could we combine things? The GT's log term is even in v, while `log(c8*exp(c9*v)+1)` is not symmetric. We can't fix this with odd/even polynomial terms since adding polynomials to an asymmetric function won't make it match a symmetric function plus polynomials across all v.

**Candidate 50:** `c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c3*sin(c1*t+c2)*cos(c4*t) + c5*sin(c6*exp(c7*v)+c8) + c9*v*Abs(v)`

The `sin(c6*exp(c7*v)+c8)` term - this is bounded between -1 and 1, so it can't reproduce the unbounded log term.

None of the candidates contain a `log(Abs(v) + const)` or `log(v**2 + const)` type term that could reproduce the logarithmic dependence on v in the GT. The `sqrt`, `exp`, polynomial, and trigonometric functions available in the candidates are fundamentally different from logarithmic functions and cannot replicate `log(Abs(v)+1)` over the full domain of v.

Even candidate 24 with its `log(c8*exp(c9*v)+1)` term cannot work because this function is monotonic in v (not even/symmetric like `log(Abs(v)+1)`), and no combination with the available polynomial terms can fix this asymmetry.

[NO MATCH]

3. A -β*log(|v| + 1) term

The key challenge is matching the **log(|v| + 1)** term. Let me analyze what functions could potentially represent this.

**log(|v| + 1) behavior:** Near v=0, log(|v|+1) ≈ |v| - v²/2 + ... For large |v|, it grows logarithmically. This is NOT a polynomial, NOT sqrt(c + v²), NOT exp(), NOT cos/sin of v.

Let me check if **sqrt(c1 + v²)** can match log(|v| + 1):
- sqrt(c1 + v²) ~ |v| for large |v| (linear growth), while log(|v|+1) grows logarithmically
- These are fundamentally different functions — they cannot be equivalent for any constant choices.

So any candidate relying solely on sqrt(c1 + v²) plus polynomials in v to capture the log term will **not** match, because:
- sqrt(c1 + v²) grows linearly for large |v|
- log(|v| + 1) grows logarithmically
- Polynomials in v grow polynomially
- No finite combination of these can equal log(|v| + 1)

This eliminates **Candidates 1-22** (all use sqrt + polynomials/trig without log).

Now let me check candidates with other structures:

**Candidate 24:** c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c3*v + c4*v³ + c5*v² + c6*v⁵ + c7*log(c8*exp(c9*v) + 1)

The term c7*log(c8*exp(c9*v) + 1) is a softplus-like function. For this to equal -β*log(|v|+1), we'd need log(c8*exp(c9*v)+1) = log(|v|+1). But exp(c9*v) is exponential while |v|+1 is not — these can't match. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidates 23, 25, 33-49:** These use polynomials in v (v, v², v³, v⁵), sin/cos terms in t, exp terms, and v*|v| terms, but none have log(|v|+1). 

Can a polynomial in v (including v*|v|, |v|, etc.) approximate log(|v|+1)? No — polynomials grow polynomially while log grows logarithmically. They are fundamentally different basis functions and cannot be exactly equal.

**Candidate 37, 39:** Include exp(c9*v²) or cos(c9*v²) — these don't match log(|v|+1) either.

**Candidate 50:** c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + c3*sin(c1*t+c2)*cos(c4*t) + c5*sin(c6*exp(c7*v)+c8) + c9*v*|v|
The sin(c6*exp(c7*v)+c8) term is bounded, while log(|v|+1) is unbounded. **NO MATCH.**

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain a log(|v|+1) term or any function that could be algebraically equivalent to it. The logarithmic dependence on v is a fundamentally different basis function from polynomials, square roots, exponentials, and trigonometric functions of v.
